Denial as Rescission in Hanafi Contract Law
States rulings on denying debt or sale and later admitting, and compares with marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that denial (juhud) of any contract except marriage constitutes rescission (faskh) and apply it to scenarios involving debt acknowledgment and sale disputes.

Core Idea
Denial of any contract except marriage is a legal rescission.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents two illustrative cases that establish a core Hanafi principle: denial (juhud) of a contract functions as an implicit rescission (faskh), except in marriage. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying contract law in Hanafi fiqh, especially when a party first denies a contract and later claims to have rescinded it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the passage and separate the first ruling (debt acknowledgment) from the second (sale denial). Note the different outcomes.
The debt case is about inconsistency in statements; the sale case is about denial of a contract.
2
Extract the general principle
The passage concludes with 'because denial of anything other than marriage is a rescission.' State this principle in Arabic and English.
This principle is the key to reconciling the two cases.
3
Understand the marriage exception
Why is marriage treated differently? Denial does not rescind marriage because of its stability and the need for formal dissolution.
This is a unique Hanafi stance; other schools differ.
4
Apply the principle to new scenarios
Given a contract type (e.g., sale, lease, marriage), determine whether denial would rescind it or not.
Always check if the contract is marriage or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال لآخر لك علي ألف فرده ثم صدقه فلا شيء عليه ومن ادعى عليه البيع فأنكر فبرهن على البيع فادعى المدعى عليه فسخه تسمع ولا يكون متناقضاً لأن جحود ما عدا النكاح فسخ هـ.
And whoever says to another, 'I owe you one thousand' and then denies it, then confirms it – nothing is upon him. And whoever is claimed against for a sale and he denies, then the claimant proves the sale, and then the defendant claims its rescission, it is heard and he is not contradictory, because denial (juhud) of anything other than marriage is a rescission. End quote.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents two compact rulings and a general principle. First: if a person says to another 'I owe you one thousand' (this is an acknowledgment), then denies it, then later confirms it (i.e., admits again), there is nothing against him – meaning his initial denial does not nullify the debt; he can still be held liable. This is because the denial itself does not cancel the debt; it only contradicts his previous statement, but the later confirmation reinstates the acknowledgment. Second: if someone is sued for a sale and the defendant denies it, but the plaintiff proves the sale with evidence, and then the defendant claims that he had rescinded the sale, his claim is heard (i.e., accepted in court) and he is not considered contradictory for having first denied and then claimed rescission. The reason is that denial (juhud) of anything other than marriage is considered a rescission (faskh). This is the principle: in contracts other than marriage, the act of denying the contract effectively rescinds it. So when the defendant initially denied the sale, that denial itself was a rescission. Therefore, his later explicit claim of rescission is consistent with the earlier denial. In marriage, denial does not rescind, so a husband who denies marriage cannot later claim rescission without contradiction. This ruling is foundational in Hanafi fiqh for understanding the effect of denial on different contracts.

Key Terms
جحود (juhud): Denial; a flat refusal to admit a claim or contract.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission; annulment of a contract ab initio.
نكاح (nikah): Marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale is unaffected; the denial is just a procedural objection.
B) The denial rescinds the sale, so a subsequent claim of rescission is not contradictory.
C) The sale becomes void ab initio.
D) The denial automatically establishes the seller's case.

Key Takeaway
Denial of any contract except marriage legally rescinds that contract in Hanafi fiqh.

The Ruling on Claiming Counterfeit Dirhams After Admission
States the ruling for admitting receipt of dirhams and claiming they were counterfeit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when an admitter is believed if he claims the dirhams were counterfeit, and distinguish between connected and separate statements.

Core Idea
The admitter is believed for zuyuf/nabahrajah; for satuqah, only if stated connectedly.

When someone admits receiving dirhams and later claims they were counterfeit, the Hanafi school has a nuanced ruling based on the type of counterfeit and how the claim is expressed. This lesson unpacks the passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, explaining the key distinctions and their legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the admitted act
The admitter says 'I received ten dirhams.' This admission is the starting point.
The admission is unconditional.
2
Determine the type of coin claimed
The admitter claims the dirhams were zuyuf, nabahrajah, or satuqah. Zuyuf are treasury-rejected, nabahrajah merchant-rejected, satuqah heavily adulterated.
The legal effect depends on which type.
3
Check if the claim was connected or separate
If the claim is in the same utterance (mawsul), it is treated as part of the admission. If later (munfasil), it is a separate claim.
The author used 'then' to indicate separate, but the ruling applies to both for zuyuf.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule
For zuyuf and nabahrajah, the admitter is believed regardless. For satuqah, he is only believed if the claim was connected.
The rationale: the term dirham applies to zuyuf and nabahrajah but not to satuqah except metaphorically.
5
Understand the consequence
If believed, he is not liable for the value. If not believed (satuqah separate), he must pay the value.
This prevents contradiction in testimony.

ومن أقر بقبض عشرة ثم ادعى إنها زيوف صدق لأن اسم الدراهم يقع على الزيوف كما يقع على الجياد والنبهرجة كالزيوف . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا بين موصولاً أو مفصولاً ولكن عبر بـ«ثم ليفيد أن البيان مفصول ليعلم حكم الموصول بالأولى. وقيد بالزيوف للاحتراز عما إذا بين أنها ستوقة فإنه لا يصدق لأن اسم الدارهم لا يقع عليها ولذا لو تجوز بالزيوف والنبهرجة في الصرف والسلم جاز وفي الستوقة لا إن كان مفصولاً، وإن كان موصولاً صدق كما في النهاية فالحاصل أنه موصولاً صحيح في الكل والتفصيل في المفصول. وقيد بإقراره بقبض عشرة لأنه لو أقر أنه قبض حقه أو الثمن أو استوفى لم يصدق للتناقض. وقيد بالدراهم لأن المشتري لو أقر أنه قبض المبيع ثم ادعى عيباً به فالقول لبائعه لأن المبيع متعين فإذا قبضه فقد أقر بأنه استوفى عين حقه دلالة فبدعواه العيب صار متناقضاً. وقيد باقتصاره على قبض الدراهم لأنه لو قال قبضت دراهم جياداً لم يصدق في دعواه الزيوف موصولاً ومفصولاً وفيها : إذا أقر أنه قبض حقه أو الثمن أو استوفى ثم ادعى : كان زيوفاً فإن كان مفصولاً لم يصدق وإلا صدق وهو المراد بما قدمناه. والفرق أن في هذه المسائل الثلاث أقر بقبض القدر والجودة بلفظ واحد فإذا استثنى الجودة كان استثناء البعض من الكل فصح موصولاً كقوله له علي ألف إلا مائة أما إذا أقر بقبض عشرة جياد فقد أقر بكل منهما بلفظ على حدة فإذا قال إلا أنها زيوف فقد استثنى الكل من الكل في حق الجودة وهو باطل كقوله له علي مائة درهم ودينار إلا ديناراً كان باطلاً وإن كان موصولاً؛ كذا في النهاية. والإقرار بقبض رأس المال كالإقرار بقبض حقه كما في البزازية. ولم يذكر المؤلف حكم وزنها عند الإطلاق والدعوى وفي كافي الحاكم : لو أقر بألف درهم عدداً ثم قال وزن خمسة أو ستة وكان الإقرار منه بالكوفة فعليه مائة درهم وزن سبعة فلا يصدق على النقصان إذا لم يبين موصولاً وكذا ،الدنانير، وإن كانوا في بلاد يتعارفون على دراهم معروفة الوزن بينهم صدق ا هـ . والزيوف ما زيفه بيت المال والنبهرجة ما يرده التجار، والستوقة - بفتح السين - ما غلب غشها فليست دراهم إلا مجازاً لأن العبرة للغالب وأطلق في الدراهم المقر بها فشمل ما إذا كانت ديناً من قرض أو ثمن مبيع أو غصباً أو وديعة ـ كما في فتح القدير - ورأس المال كذلك - كما في البزازية - وقيد بدعوى المقر لأنه لو أقر بقبض دراهم معينة ثم مات فادعى وارثه أنها زيوف لم تقبل، وكذا إذا أقر بالوديعة والمضاربة أو الغصب ثم زعم الوارث أنها زيوف لم يصدق الوارث لأنه صار ديناً في مال الميت؛ كذا في البزازية : وفيها من الرهن : قضى دينه وبعضه زيوف وستوقة فرهن شيئاً بالستوقة والزيوف وقال خذه رهناً بما فيه من زيوف وستوق صح في حق الستوق لأنها ليست من الجنس ولا يصح في الزيوف لأنها من الجنس فلا دین اهـ. وقيد بالإقرار بالقبض لأنه لو أقر بألف ولم يبين الجهة ثم ادعى موصولاً أنها زيف لم يقض عليه. واختلف المشايخ قيل أيضاً على الخلاف، وقيل يصدق بالإجماع لأن الجودة تجب في بعض الوجوه لا على البعض فلا تجب بالاحتمال. ولو قال غصبت ألفاً أو أودعني ألفاً إلا أنها زيوف صدق وإن فصل. وعن الإمام أن القرض كالغصب. ولو قال في الغصب والوديعة إلا أنها رصاص أو ستوقة صدق إذا وصل، ولو قال على كر حنطة من ثمن مبيع أو قرض إلا أنه رديء فالقول له، وليس هذا كدعوي الرداءة لأن الرداءة في الحنطة ليست بعيب لأن العيب ما يخلو عنه أصل الفطرة والحنطة قد تكون رديئة بأصل الخلقة فلا يطلق عليه مطلقه على الجيد، ولذا لم يجز شراء البر بدون ذكر الصفة، أقر بقرض عشرة أفلس أو ثمن مبيع ثم ادعى أنها كاسدة لم يصدق وإن وصل. وقالا : يصدق في القرض إذا وصل أما في البيع فلا يصدق عند الثاني في قوله الأول. وقال محمد يصدق في البيع وعليه قيمة المبيع. وكذا الخلاف في قوله علي عشرة ستوقة من قرض أو ثمن المبيع. ولو قال غصبته عشرة أفلس أو أودعني عشرة أفلس ثم نت قال المسلم إليه ؛ كذا في البزازية. وذكر في القنية مسألة ما إذا أقر بدين ثم ادعى أن بعضه قرض وبعضه ربا أنه يقبل فيه إذا برهن وذكره عبد القادر في الطبقات من الألقاب عن علاء الدين .
And whoever admits receiving ten dirhams then claims they were counterfeit is believed because the name dirham applies to counterfeit as it applies to good and to nabahrajah (which is like counterfeit). He (the author) left it unrestricted so it includes whether he stated it connectedly or separately, but he expressed it with 'then' to indicate that the statement is separate so that the ruling of the connected is known by priority. And he restricted it to counterfeit to exclude if he states it was satuqah, for then he is not believed because the name dirham does not apply to them. Hence, if one transacts in counterfeit and nabahrajah in currency exchange and salam, it is permissible, but in satuqah it is not if separate; if connected, he is believed as in al-Nihayah. So the result: connected is valid in all, and detail is in separate. And he restricted it to his admission of receiving ten because if he admitted that he received his right or the price or received full payment, he is not believed due to contradiction. And he restricted to dirhams because if the buyer admits receiving the sold item then claims a defect, the seller's word is taken because the sold item is specific; when he received it, he implicitly admitted receiving the very object of his right, so his claim of defect makes him contradictory. And he restricted to his limiting to receipt of dirhams because if he said 'I received good dirhams', he is not believed in his claim of counterfeitness whether connected or separate. And in it: if he admitted that he received his right or the price or received full payment then claimed they were counterfeit, if separate he is not believed, otherwise he is believed; that is what we presented. The difference is that in these three cases he admitted receipt of quantity and quality with one wording; so when he excepts quality, it is excepting part from the whole, so it is valid connected like his saying 'I owe a thousand except a hundred'. But if he admitted receipt of ten good dirhams, he admitted each with a separate wording; so when he says 'except they are counterfeit', he excepts the whole from the whole regarding quality, and it is invalid like his saying 'I owe a hundred dirhams and a dinar except a dinar' is invalid even if connected; thus in al-Nihayah. And admission of receipt of capital is like admission of receipt of his right as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And the author did not mention the ruling of weight when unrestricted and claim. And in Kafi al-Hakim: if one admits to a thousand dirhams by number then says weight of five or six, and the admission was in Kufa, then he owes a hundred dirhams by weight of seven, so he is not believed regarding the deficiency if he did not state it connectedly; likewise dinars; and if they are in a land where they are accustomed to dirhams of known weight among them, he is believed. End. And counterfeit (zuyuf) is what the treasury has rejected, and nabahrajah is what merchants reject, and satuqah is that whose adulteration predominates, so they are not dirhams except metaphorically because consideration is for the predominant. And he (the author) was unrestricted regarding the dirhams admitted, so it includes whether they were a debt from loan or price of sale or usurpation or deposit as in Fath al-Qadir, and capital likewise as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And he restricted to the claim of the admitter because if he admitted receipt of specific dirhams then died and his heir claimed they were counterfeit, it is not accepted; likewise if he admitted deposit or partnership or usurpation then the heir claimed they were counterfeit, the heir is not believed because it became a debt in the deceased's estate; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. And in it from the chapter of pledge: he paid his debt, part of which was counterfeit and satuqah, then pledged something with the satuqah and counterfeit and said 'Take it as pledge for what is in it of counterfeit and satuqah' — it is valid regarding the satuqah because it is not of the same genus, and invalid regarding the counterfeit because it is of the same genus, so no debt. End. And he restricted to admission of receipt because if he admitted to a thousand without specifying the source, then claimed connectedly that they were counterfeit, he is not ruled against. And the scholars differed: some said it is also upon the disagreement, and some said he is believed by consensus because quality is mandatory in some ways not all, so it is not mandatory by probability. And if he said 'I usurped a thousand' or 'he deposited a thousand with me except that they were counterfeit', he is believed even if separate. And from Imam Abu Hanifa that loan is like usurpation. And if he said in usurpation and deposit 'except that they were lead or satuqah', he is believed if connected. And if he said 'Upon me a load of wheat from price of sale or loan except that it is poor quality', the statement is his; and this is not like a claim of poor quality because poor quality in wheat is not a defect because a defect is what is free from original nature, and wheat may be poor quality by original creation, so its absolute is not applied to good; hence purchase of wheat without mentioning description is not permissible. If he admitted to a loan of ten worthless coins or price of sale then claimed they were worthless, he is not believed even if connected. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is believed in the loan if connected, but in the sale he is not believed according to the second (Abu Yusuf) in his first statement. And Muhammad said he is believed in the sale and is liable for the value of the sold item. Likewise the disagreement in his saying 'Upon me ten satuqah from loan or price of sale.' And if he said 'I usurped ten worthless coins' or 'he deposited ten worthless coins with me' then ... said the Muslim to him; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. And it is mentioned in al-Qunyah a case: if one admits a debt then claims that part of it is loan and part is usury, it is accepted if he provides proof; mentioned by Abdul Qadir in al-Tabaqat from al-Ala' al-Din.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on when a person who admits receiving dirhams is believed if he later claims they were counterfeit. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the conditions based on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The basic rule: if someone admits receiving ten dirhams and then says they were counterfeit (zuyuf), he is believed because the term 'dirhams' includes counterfeit coins linguistically. However, this is restricted: if he claims they were satuqah (heavily adulterated), he is not believed if he says it separately (munfasil) because such coins are not called dirhams except metaphorically; if he said it connectedly (mawsul, e.g., 'I received ten dirhams that are satuqah'), he is believed. The distinction between mawsul and munfasil is crucial: when the statement is connected, the exception is part of the original admission and is valid; when separate, it is a separate claim and may be contradictory. The passage then discusses various applications: admitting receipt of a specific right, admitting receipt of the sold item, admitting receipt of good dirhams, etc. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding worthless coins (afilas) or bad dirhams: Abu Hanifa holds that the admitter is not believed whether connected or separate; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he is believed in a loan if connected, but in a sale there is disagreement between them. The passage also covers cases of usurpation, deposit, and even a case of pledge. The definition of terms: zuyuf are coins rejected by the treasury, nabahrajah are those rejected by merchants, and satuqah are those with predominant adulteration. The ruling is based on linguistic usage and avoidance of contradiction. This is a standard Hanafi position from the Zahir al-Riwayah, with later refinements.

Key Terms
زيوف (zuyūf): Counterfeit dirhams that have been rejected by the treasury (Bayt al-Mal).
نبهرجة (nabahrajah): Coins rejected by merchants, probably of lower quality but still circulating.
ستوقة (satūqah): Coins with predominant adulteration (ghash) to the extent that they are no longer called dirhams except metaphorically.
موصول (mawṣūl): A statement where the exception or qualification is made in the same utterance without a break (e.g., 'I received ten dirhams, but they are counterfeit').
مفصول (munfaṣil): A statement where the exception is made in a separate utterance after the admission (e.g., first 'I received ten dirhams', then later 'they were counterfeit').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person admits receiving ten dirhams and later says: 'They were satuqah.' If this statement was made in a separate conversation (munfasil), is he believed?
A) Yes, because the term dirham includes all types.
B) No, because satuqah are not called dirhams.
C) Yes, because the admission is his word.
D) No, because he changed his mind.

Key Takeaway
The admitter is believed for zuyuf/nabahrajah; for satuqah, only if stated connectedly.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
8 min
The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Worthless Coins in Admissions
Discusses the disagreement on worthless coins in admissions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding claims of worthless coins (afilas/kasad) and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa rejects all claims of worthless coins; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept in loan if connected, but differ on sale.

When an admitter claims the dirhams were worthless (kasad or afilas), the Hanafi imams split. This lesson examines each view and the practical consequences for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person admits receiving dirhams as a loan or as a price of sale. Later he claims the dirhams were worthless (afilas/kasad) or satuqah.
The dispute centers on whether he is believed.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the admitter is not believed whether the claim is connected or separate. The admission of receipt implies standard value.
This is his view for both loan and sale.
3
State the position of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)
In a loan, if the claim is connected, he is believed. In a sale, Abu Yusuf does not believe him; Muhammad believes him but he must pay the value of the sold item.
Muhammad's view is that the claim is valid but does not negate liability.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Hanifa sees a contradiction in admitting receipt of dirhams and then denying their value. The two see that a loan is different from a sale: in a loan, the debtor is only liable for the value, so claiming worthlessness avoids contradiction; in a sale, the price is a specific asset, so claiming worthlessness contradicts.
Muhammad allows it in sale but requires compensation to avoid injustice.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi practice tends to follow the two in loan, and Muhammad's view in sale is considered stronger by some, though others maintain Abu Yusuf's position.
The passage does not give a definitive tarjih; it presents the ikhtilaf.

ومن أقر بقبض عشرة ثم ادعى إنها زيوف صدق لأن اسم الدراهم يقع على الزيوف كما يقع على الجياد والنبهرجة كالزيوف . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا بين موصولاً أو مفصولاً ولكن عبر بـ«ثم ليفيد أن البيان مفصول ليعلم حكم الموصول بالأولى. وقيد بالزيوف للاحتراز عما إذا بين أنها ستوقة فإنه لا يصدق لأن اسم الدارهم لا يقع عليها ولذا لو تجوز بالزيوف والنبهرجة في الصرف والسلم جاز وفي الستوقة لا إن كان مفصولاً، وإن كان موصولاً صدق كما في النهاية فالحاصل أنه موصولاً صحيح في الكل والتفصيل في المفصول. وقيد بإقراره بقبض عشرة لأنه لو أقر أنه قبض حقه أو الثمن أو استوفى لم يصدق للتناقض. وقيد بالدراهم لأن المشتري لو أقر أنه قبض المبيع ثم ادعى عيباً به فالقول لبائعه لأن المبيع متعين فإذا قبضه فقد أقر بأنه استوفى عين حقه دلالة فبدعواه العيب صار متناقضاً. وقيد باقتصاره على قبض الدراهم لأنه لو قال قبضت دراهم جياداً لم يصدق في دعواه الزيوف موصولاً ومفصولاً وفيها : إذا أقر أنه قبض حقه أو الثمن أو استوفى ثم ادعى : كان زيوفاً فإن كان مفصولاً لم يصدق وإلا صدق وهو المراد بما قدمناه. والفرق أن في هذه المسائل الثلاث أقر بقبض القدر والجودة بلفظ واحد فإذا استثنى الجودة كان استثناء البعض من الكل فصح موصولاً كقوله له علي ألف إلا مائة أما إذا أقر بقبض عشرة جياد فقد أقر بكل منهما بلفظ على حدة فإذا قال إلا أنها زيوف فقد استثنى الكل من الكل في حق الجودة وهو باطل كقوله له علي مائة درهم ودينار إلا ديناراً كان باطلاً وإن كان موصولاً؛ كذا في النهاية. والإقرار بقبض رأس المال كالإقرار بقبض حقه كما في البزازية. ولم يذكر المؤلف حكم وزنها عند الإطلاق والدعوى وفي كافي الحاكم : لو أقر بألف درهم عدداً ثم قال وزن خمسة أو ستة وكان الإقرار منه بالكوفة فعليه مائة درهم وزن سبعة فلا يصدق على النقصان إذا لم يبين موصولاً وكذا ،الدنانير، وإن كانوا في بلاد يتعارفون على دراهم معروفة الوزن بينهم صدق ا هـ . والزيوف ما زيفه بيت المال والنبهرجة ما يرده التجار، والستوقة - بفتح السين - ما غلب غشها فليست دراهم إلا مجازاً لأن العبرة للغالب وأطلق في الدراهم المقر بها فشمل ما إذا كانت ديناً من قرض أو ثمن مبيع أو غصباً أو وديعة ـ كما في فتح القدير - ورأس المال كذلك - كما في البزازية - وقيد بدعوى المقر لأنه لو أقر بقبض دراهم معينة ثم مات فادعى وارثه أنها زيوف لم تقبل، وكذا إذا أقر بالوديعة والمضاربة أو الغصب ثم زعم الوارث أنها زيوف لم يصدق الوارث لأنه صار ديناً في مال الميت؛ كذا في البزازية : وفيها من الرهن : قضى دينه وبعضه زيوف وستوقة فرهن شيئاً بالستوقة والزيوف وقال خذه رهناً بما فيه من زيوف وستوق صح في حق الستوق لأنها ليست من الجنس ولا يصح في الزيوف لأنها من الجنس فلا دین اهـ. وقيد بالإقرار بالقبض لأنه لو أقر بألف ولم يبين الجهة ثم ادعى موصولاً أنها زيف لم يقض عليه. واختلف المشايخ قيل أيضاً على الخلاف، وقيل يصدق بالإجماع لأن الجودة تجب في بعض الوجوه لا على البعض فلا تجب بالاحتمال. ولو قال غصبت ألفاً أو أودعني ألفاً إلا أنها زيوف صدق وإن فصل. وعن الإمام أن القرض كالغصب. ولو قال في الغصب والوديعة إلا أنها رصاص أو ستوقة صدق إذا وصل، ولو قال على كر حنطة من ثمن مبيع أو قرض إلا أنه رديء فالقول له، وليس هذا كدعوي الرداءة لأن الرداءة في الحنطة ليست بعيب لأن العيب ما يخلو عنه أصل الفطرة والحنطة قد تكون رديئة بأصل الخلقة فلا يطلق عليه مطلقه على الجيد، ولذا لم يجز شراء البر بدون ذكر الصفة، أقر بقرض عشرة أفلس أو ثمن مبيع ثم ادعى أنها كاسدة لم يصدق وإن وصل. وقالا : يصدق في القرض إذا وصل أما في البيع فلا يصدق عند الثاني في قوله الأول. وقال محمد يصدق في البيع وعليه قيمة المبيع. وكذا الخلاف في قوله علي عشرة ستوقة من قرض أو ثمن المبيع. ولو قال غصبته عشرة أفلس أو أودعني عشرة أفلس ثم نت قال المسلم إليه ؛ كذا في البزازية. وذكر في القنية مسألة ما إذا أقر بدين ثم ادعى أن بعضه قرض وبعضه ربا أنه يقبل فيه إذا برهن وذكره عبد القادر في الطبقات من الألقاب عن علاء الدين .
And whoever admits receiving ten dirhams then claims they were counterfeit is believed because the name dirham applies to counterfeit as it applies to good and to nabahrajah (which is like counterfeit). He (the author) left it unrestricted so it includes whether he stated it connectedly or separately, but he expressed it with 'then' to indicate that the statement is separate so that the ruling of the connected is known by priority. And he restricted it to counterfeit to exclude if he states it was satuqah, for then he is not believed because the name dirham does not apply to them. Hence, if one transacts in counterfeit and nabahrajah in currency exchange and salam, it is permissible, but in satuqah it is not if separate; if connected, he is believed as in al-Nihayah. So the result: connected is valid in all, and detail is in separate. And he restricted it to his admission of receiving ten because if he admitted that he received his right or the price or received full payment, he is not believed due to contradiction. And he restricted to dirhams because if the buyer admits receiving the sold item then claims a defect, the seller's word is taken because the sold item is specific; when he received it, he implicitly admitted receiving the very object of his right, so his claim of defect makes him contradictory. And he restricted to his limiting to receipt of dirhams because if he said 'I received good dirhams', he is not believed in his claim of counterfeitness whether connected or separate. And in it: if he admitted that he received his right or the price or received full payment then claimed they were counterfeit, if separate he is not believed, otherwise he is believed; that is what we presented. The difference is that in these three cases he admitted receipt of quantity and quality with one wording; so when he excepts quality, it is excepting part from the whole, so it is valid connected like his saying 'I owe a thousand except a hundred'. But if he admitted receipt of ten good dirhams, he admitted each with a separate wording; so when he says 'except they are counterfeit', he excepts the whole from the whole regarding quality, and it is invalid like his saying 'I owe a hundred dirhams and a dinar except a dinar' is invalid even if connected; thus in al-Nihayah. And admission of receipt of capital is like admission of receipt of his right as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And the author did not mention the ruling of weight when unrestricted and claim. And in Kafi al-Hakim: if one admits to a thousand dirhams by number then says weight of five or six, and the admission was in Kufa, then he owes a hundred dirhams by weight of seven, so he is not believed regarding the deficiency if he did not state it connectedly; likewise dinars; and if they are in a land where they are accustomed to dirhams of known weight among them, he is believed. End. And counterfeit (zuyuf) is what the treasury has rejected, and nabahrajah is what merchants reject, and satuqah is that whose adulteration predominates, so they are not dirhams except metaphorically because consideration is for the predominant. And he (the author) was unrestricted regarding the dirhams admitted, so it includes whether they were a debt from loan or price of sale or usurpation or deposit as in Fath al-Qadir, and capital likewise as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And he restricted to the claim of the admitter because if he admitted receipt of specific dirhams then died and his heir claimed they were counterfeit, it is not accepted; likewise if he admitted deposit or partnership or usurpation then the heir claimed they were counterfeit, the heir is not believed because it became a debt in the deceased's estate; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. And in it from the chapter of pledge: he paid his debt, part of which was counterfeit and satuqah, then pledged something with the satuqah and counterfeit and said 'Take it as pledge for what is in it of counterfeit and satuqah' — it is valid regarding the satuqah because it is not of the same genus, and invalid regarding the counterfeit because it is of the same genus, so no debt. End. And he restricted to admission of receipt because if he admitted to a thousand without specifying the source, then claimed connectedly that they were counterfeit, he is not ruled against. And the scholars differed: some said it is also upon the disagreement, and some said he is believed by consensus because quality is mandatory in some ways not all, so it is not mandatory by probability. And if he said 'I usurped a thousand' or 'he deposited a thousand with me except that they were counterfeit', he is believed even if separate. And from Imam Abu Hanifa that loan is like usurpation. And if he said in usurpation and deposit 'except that they were lead or satuqah', he is believed if connected. And if he said 'Upon me a load of wheat from price of sale or loan except that it is poor quality', the statement is his; and this is not like a claim of poor quality because poor quality in wheat is not a defect because a defect is what is free from original nature, and wheat may be poor quality by original creation, so its absolute is not applied to good; hence purchase of wheat without mentioning description is not permissible. If he admitted to a loan of ten worthless coins or price of sale then claimed they were worthless, he is not believed even if connected. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is believed in the loan if connected, but in the sale he is not believed according to the second (Abu Yusuf) in his first statement. And Muhammad said he is believed in the sale and is liable for the value of the sold item. Likewise the disagreement in his saying 'Upon me ten satuqah from loan or price of sale.' And if he said 'I usurped ten worthless coins' or 'he deposited ten worthless coins with me' then ... said the Muslim to him; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. And it is mentioned in al-Qunyah a case: if one admits a debt then claims that part of it is loan and part is usury, it is accepted if he provides proof; mentioned by Abdul Qadir in al-Tabaqat from al-Ala' al-Din.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on when a person who admits receiving dirhams is believed if he later claims they were counterfeit. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the conditions based on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The basic rule: if someone admits receiving ten dirhams and then says they were counterfeit (zuyuf), he is believed because the term 'dirhams' includes counterfeit coins linguistically. However, this is restricted: if he claims they were satuqah (heavily adulterated), he is not believed if he says it separately (munfasil) because such coins are not called dirhams except metaphorically; if he said it connectedly (mawsul, e.g., 'I received ten dirhams that are satuqah'), he is believed. The distinction between mawsul and munfasil is crucial: when the statement is connected, the exception is part of the original admission and is valid; when separate, it is a separate claim and may be contradictory. The passage then discusses various applications: admitting receipt of a specific right, admitting receipt of the sold item, admitting receipt of good dirhams, etc. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding worthless coins (afilas) or bad dirhams: Abu Hanifa holds that the admitter is not believed whether connected or separate; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he is believed in a loan if connected, but in a sale there is disagreement between them. The passage also covers cases of usurpation, deposit, and even a case of pledge. The definition of terms: zuyuf are coins rejected by the treasury, nabahrajah are those rejected by merchants, and satuqah are those with predominant adulteration. The ruling is based on linguistic usage and avoidance of contradiction. This is a standard Hanafi position from the Zahir al-Riwayah, with later refinements.

Key Terms
أفلس (aflas): Singular of afilas: worthless dirhams, coins of no value.
كاسد (kāsid): Worthless or unsalable; often used interchangeably with afilas.
زيوف (zuyūf): Counterfeit dirhams rejected by treasury.
ستوقة (satūqah): Heavily adulterated coins not considered dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a loan, if the admitter claims the dirhams were worthless (афлис) and the claim is connected, which Hanafi imam does NOT believe him?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has internal disagreement on worthless coin claims; follow the two in loan and Muhammad in sale.

The Ruling on Contradictory Admissions in Debt
Ruling on contradictory admissions compared to contract rescission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on contradictory admissions in debt cases and apply the distinction between unilateral rejection of an admission and rescission of a contract.

Core Idea
A debtor can unilaterally reject a debt admission, but the creditor's later confirmation is just a claim, not binding.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where a creditor first claims a debt, the debtor returns it, and then the creditor confirms the return. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling that distinguishes between unilateral rejection of an admission and rescission of a contract. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly handling contradictory statements in financial disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the initial ruling: if a creditor says 'You owe me a thousand', the debtor returns it, then the creditor confirms, nothing is due on the debtor. Note the key terms: 'radd al-iqrar' (rejection of admission) and 'tasdiq' (confirmation).
The ruling is clear: the debtor owes nothing.
2
Trace the Reasoning in al-Hidayah
Understand the reasoning: the initial admission is overruled by the debtor's return; the confirmation is a claim requiring proof or opponent's admission. Contrast with contract rescission: one party cannot unilaterally rescind a contract because it belongs to both.
The debtor's unilateral rejection is unique to admissions.
3
Analyze the Critique from al-Kafi
Identify the objection: in a previous ruling (issue of denial), the same author allowed unilateral rescission when receiving the price becomes impossible. This seems contradictory. Understand the apparent inconsistency.
The critique points to a potential conflict between two rulings.
4
Examine the Response in Fath al-Qadir
See how the author defends the ruling: the previous case is different because rescission is allowed when consent is lost or impossibility arises. The two cases are distinguished by the nature of the right (individual vs. contractual).
The response upholds the original ruling but clarifies the boundary.
5
Evaluate the Final Position
Conclude that the Hanafi position remains: the debtor's unilateral rejection is valid, while the creditor's confirmation is a claim. The apparent contradiction is resolved by distinguishing between rights that belong solely to one party versus contract rights shared by both.
This lesson refines your understanding of iqrar and contract law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن قال لآخر لك علي ألف فرده ثم صدقه فلا شيء عليه) لأن إقراره هو الأول وقد ارتد برد المقر له والثاني دعوى فلا بد من الحجة أو تصديق الخصم بخلاف ما إذا قال اشتريت وأنكر له أن يصدقه لأن أحد العاقدين لا ينفرد بالفسخ كما لا ينفرد بالعقد، والمعنى أنه حقهما فبقي العقد فعمل التصديق أما المقر له فينفرد برد الإقرار فافترقا ؛ كذا الهداية. وناقضه في الكافي بأنه ذكر هنا أن أحد المتعاقدين لا ينفرد بالفسخ وفيما تقدم يعني في مسألة التجاحد قال : ولأنه لما تعذر استيفاء الثمن من المشتري فات رضا البائع فيستبد بالفسخ والترفيق بين کلامه صعب ا هـ . وأقره عليه في فتح القدير بقوله بعده وهو صحيح ويقتضي أنه لو تعذر الاستيفاء مع الإقرار بأن مات ولا بينة أن له أن يفسخ ويستمتع بالجارية قوله: (فلا بد من الحجة) قال في الحواشي السعدية : كيف تقبل حجته وهو متناقض في دعواه
His saying: (And whoever says to another 'You owe me a thousand' and the debtor returns it to him, then he (the creditor) confirms it, then nothing is due upon him) because his (the creditor's) admission is the first and it is overruled by the return by the one admitted to (the debtor), and the second (the confirmation) is a claim, so proof or the opponent's confirmation is needed. Unlike if he said 'I bought' and the other denies, he (the buyer) cannot confirm him (the seller) to effect rescission because one of the two contracting parties cannot unilaterally rescind just as he cannot unilaterally conclude the contract. The meaning: it is the right of both, so the contract remains, so the confirmation does not work. As for the one admitted to (the debtor), he can unilaterally reject the admission, so they differ. Thus in al-Hidayah. And al-Kafi contradicted him because he mentioned here that one of the two contractors cannot unilaterally rescind, while previously in the issue of denial he said: 'Because when receiving the price from the buyer becomes impossible, the seller's consent is lost, so he may independently rescind.' Reconciling his words is difficult. And he (the author of al-Hidayah) confirmed it in Fath al-Qadir with his statement after it: 'And it is valid and implies that if receipt is impossible despite admission due to death and no evidence, he may rescind and enjoy the slave-girl.' His saying: 'So proof is needed.' He said in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah: 'How can his proof be accepted when he is contradictory in his claim?'
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on a scenario where a creditor first declares a debt, then the debtor returns the debt (perhaps pays or hands over something), and then the creditor confirms that the debt is indeed fulfilled. The ruling: nothing is due on the debtor. The reasoning: the creditor's initial admission of debt is the basis, but that admission is overruled (irtadda) by the debtor's return (radd). The subsequent confirmation by the creditor is merely a claim (da'wa), which is not binding without proof or the opponent's confirmation (tasdiq). The passage compares this to a contract rescission: a buyer who claims to have bought cannot unilaterally rescind by merely saying so, because both parties have rights in the contract. However, a debtor can unilaterally reject an admission of debt because the admission is a declaration in his favor, and he can waive it. There is a critique from al-Kafi: the author of al-Hidayah said elsewhere that one contractor can unilaterally rescind if receiving the price becomes impossible (e.g., buyer dies without evidence), which seems contradictory. The author of Fath al-Qadir then suggests this is valid, allowing rescission in such cases. The passage ends with a question from the Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah: how can his proof be accepted if he is contradictory? This implies that the confirmation is contradictory to the initial admission, so proof is needed to resolve the contradiction. This is a nuanced ruling within Hanafi fiqh about the effect of admissions and the ability to unilaterally rescind certain declarations.

Key Terms
رد الإقرار (radd al-iqrār): The debtor's rejection or return of the creditor's admission (i.e., the debtor acts contrary to the admission).
تصديق (taṣdīq): Confirmation by the creditor that the debt has been fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can the debtor unilaterally reject the admission while a buyer cannot unilaterally rescind a sale contract?
A) Because the admission is a unilateral right of the debtor, while the contract is a mutual right.
B) Because the debtor is considered the owner of the debt.
C) Because the buyer has more rights than the debtor.
D) Because the contract is written, while the admission is oral.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a debtor can unilaterally reject an admission of debt by returning it, but a creditor's later confirmation is merely a claim, not a binding admission.

General Principle and Pledge with Counterfeit Coins
Rulings on acknowledgment of debt with counterfeit coins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on a debtor's claim that the acknowledged debt was in counterfeit coins and apply it to pledge scenarios.

Core Idea
A debtor's claim of poor quality coins is only accepted if specified at the time of acknowledgment.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between the genus (jins) of coins when a debtor later claims they were counterfeit. This lesson covers the foundational rule for such claims and its application to pledges (rahn), where the validity of the pledge depends on whether the coins are of the same currency type.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule for heir's claim
Read the first ruling: if an heir claims that the debt owed to the deceased was in counterfeit coins, the heir is not believed. Why? Because the debt is already fixed against the estate.
This establishes that a mere later claim without upfront specification is ineffective.
2
Analyze the pledge scenario
Consider the case where a man pays part of his debt with counterfeit and base coins, then pledges an item for those coins. The pledge is valid for base coins (sutuqa) because they are a different genus, but invalid for counterfeit (ziyuf) because they share the same genus as the debt currency.
The key distinction: genus determines riba treatment and pledge validity.
3
Apply the condition of specification
Note that the debtor's claim of counterfeits is only accepted if he specified it at the time of acknowledgment (connected, mawsulan). Without that, the claim is ignored.
This condition applies across all scenarios in this lesson.

زعم الوارث أنها زيوف لم يصدق الوارث لأنه صار ديناً في مال الميت؛ كذا في البزازية : وفيها من الرهن : قضى دينه وبعضه زيوف وستوقة فرهن شيئاً بالستوقة والزيوف وقال خذه رهناً بما فيه من زيوف وستوق صح في حق الستوق لأنها ليست من الجنس ولا يصح في الزيوف لأنها من الجنس فلا دین اهـ. وقيد بالإقرار بالقبض لأنه لو أقر بألف ولم يبين الجهة ثم ادعى موصولاً أنها زيف لم يقض عليه. واختلف المشايخ قيل أيضاً على الخلاف، وقيل يصدق بالإجماع لأن الجودة تجب في بعض الوجوه لا على البعض فلا تجب بالاحتمال. ولو قال غصبت ألفاً أو أودعني ألفاً إلا أنها زيوف صدق وإن فصل. وعن الإمام أن القرض كالغصب. ولو قال في الغصب والوديعة إلا أنها رصاص أو ستوقة صدق إذا وصل، ولو قال على كر حنطة من ثمن مبيع أو قرض إلا أنه رديء فالقول له، وليس هذا كدعوي الرداءة لأن الرداءة في الحنطة ليست بعيب لأن العيب ما يخلو عنه أصل الفطرة والحنطة قد تكون رديئة بأصل الخلقة فلا يطلق عليه مطلقه على الجيد، ولذا لم يجز شراء البر بدون ذكر الصفة، أقر بقرض عشرة أفلس أو ثمن مبيع ثم ادعى أنها كاسدة لم يصدق وإن وصل. وقالا : يصدق في القرض إذا وصل أما في البيع فلا يصدق عند الثاني في قوله الأول. وقال محمد يصدق في البيع وعليه قيمة المبيع. وكذا الخلاف في قوله علي عشرة ستوقة من قرض أو ثمن المبيع. ولو قال غصبته عشرة أفلس أو أودعني عشرة أفلس ثم قال هي كاسدة صدق المسلم إليه؛ كذا في البزازية. وذكر في القنية مسألة ما إذا أقر بدين ثم ادعى أن بعضه قرض وبعضه ربا أنه يقبل فيه إذا برهن وذكره عبد القادر في الطبقات من الألقاب عن علاء الدين.
Book of Transfer of Debt, Chapter of Arbitration
63
If the heir claims they are counterfeit, the heir is not believed because it has become a debt in the deceased's estate; so in al-Bazzaziyya: And in it from the chapter of pledge: He paid his debt and part of it was counterfeit and base coins, and he pledged something for the base and counterfeit ones and said 'Take it as a pledge for what is in it of counterfeit and base' — it is valid regarding the base coin because it is not of the same type, and not valid regarding the counterfeit because it is of the same type, so no debt. End. And it is conditioned by acknowledgment of receipt because if he acknowledged a thousand without specifying the category then later claimed that it was counterfeit when connected, he is not judged against him. And the scholars differed: some said it is also on the difference, and some said he is believed by consensus because quality is obligatory in some ways not in all, so it is not obligatory by probability. And if he said 'I usurped a thousand' or 'deposited with me a thousand except that they are counterfeit' he is believed even if detailed. And from the Imam that a loan is like usurpation. And if he said in usurpation and deposit 'except they are lead or base coin' he is believed if connected. And if he said 'upon me a kurr of wheat from sale price or loan except that it is poor quality' then his word is accepted, and this is not like a claim of defectiveness because defectiveness in wheat is not a defect since a defect is what is absent from original nature, and wheat may be of poor quality by original creation, so its absolute term does not apply to good quality, and for this reason buying wheat without specifying the quality is not permissible. He acknowledged a loan of ten coins or a sale price then claimed they were worthless — he is not believed even if connected. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is believed in the loan if connected; as for sale, he is not believed according to the second in his first statement. And Muhammad said he is believed in sale and owes the value of what was sold. And similarly the dispute in his saying 'upon me ten base coins from loan or sale price'. And if he said 'I usurped ten coins' or 'deposited with me ten coins' then said 'they are worthless' — the depositor is believed; so in al-Bazzaziyya. And it is mentioned in al-Qunyah the issue of when one acknowledges a debt then claims that part of it is a loan and part is riba — that it is accepted if he proves it, and Abd al-Qadir mentioned it in al-Tabaqat from the titles of Ala al-Din.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, presents several rulings regarding an acknowledgment (iqrar) of debt where the debtor later claims the coins are counterfeit (ziyuf) or defective. The opening rule: if an heir claims that the debt owed to the deceased was in counterfeit coins, the heir is not believed because the debt has already become a claim against the estate. The ruling is from al-Bazzaziyya. The text then discusses a scenario involving a pledge (rahn) where part payment was in counterfeit and part in base coins (sutuqa). The validity of taking such a pledge varies: permissible for base coins (not of the same currency type) but not for counterfeit (same type). The general principle is that if the debtor acknowledges a debt without specifying the quality, then later claims it was of poor quality, his claim is only accepted if he mentioned it at the time of acknowledgment (connected, mawsulan). There is a difference of opinion: some scholars say he is still not believed, but the preferred view is that he is believed by consensus because quality is only obligatory in certain ways. Specific cases: usurpation (ghasb) and deposit (wadi'ah) - if he says 'except they are counterfeit' he is believed if connected. Imam Abu Hanifa equates loan to usurpation. For wheat, if he acknowledges a sale price or loan but says it was poor quality, his word is accepted because poor quality is not a defect in wheat. However, if he acknowledges a loan of coins then claims they were worthless (kasida), he is not believed unless connected; the two companions (Sahibayn) distinguish between loan (believed if connected) and sale (not believed). Muhammad al-Shaybani holds he is believed in sale but must pay the value. The same dispute applies to base coins. Finally, if one acknowledges a debt then claims part is loan part riba, it is accepted only with proof.

Key Terms
زيوف (ziyūf): Counterfeit coins that are of the same type as genuine currency but defective.
ستوقة (sutūqa): Base metal coins of a different type than standard currency.
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment of a right or debt against oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a debtor acknowledges a debt without specifying the quality of the coins and later claims they were counterfeit, what is the ruling?
A) He is believed because he is the debtor.
B) He is not believed because he did not specify at the time of acknowledgment.
C) He is believed only if the creditor admits it.
D) He is believed only if he produces a witness.

Key Takeaway
An after-the-fact claim that a debt was in counterfeit coins is only accepted if the debtor specified the quality at the time of acknowledgment.

Specific Cases: Usurpation, Deposit, Wheat, Loan, and Sale
Rulings on claims of defective coins in various transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on claims of defective coins and goods in usurpation, deposit, and sale/loan contexts, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
In usurpation and deposit, claims of counterfeits are accepted if connected; in sale and loan, there is ikhtilaf between the Hanafi imams.

The passage moves from general principles to specific transactions: usurpation (ghasb), deposit (wadi'ah), sale of wheat, and loan/sale of coins. Each scenario has distinct rules. The Hanafi master's views diverge on whether the debtor is believed when claiming the coins were worthless (kasida). This lesson unpacks these nuanced positions and shows how to apply them.

Guided Path
1
Analyze usurpation and deposit cases
If someone says 'I usurped a thousand' or 'deposited with me a thousand except that they are counterfeit' and he 'connected' the claim (mentioned it right after), he is believed. This applies even if the coins are lead or base.
The principle: in trust- or tort-based obligations, the claimant's word on quality is accepted if timely.
2
Examine the wheat scenario
If someone acknowledges a debt of a kurr of wheat from a sale or loan and says 'except it is of poor quality', his word is accepted because poor quality is not a defect in wheat—wheat can be inherently inferior.
This is distinguished from a claim of defect 'ayb', which would require proof.
3
Understand the loan/sale of coins dispute
For a loan of coins later claimed worthless: Abu Hanifa does not accept even if connected. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept in loan if connected. In sale, Abu Yusuf does not accept; Muhammad accepts but requires payment of value.
The same dispute applies to base coins (sutuqa). Memorize the three positions.
4
Apply to acknowledgment split between loan and riba
If someone acknowledges a debt then claims part is loan, part riba, it is accepted only if he provides proof (burhan).
This is a different category because riba is prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحوالة باب التحكيم
٦٣
زعم الوارث أنها زيوف لم يصدق الوارث لأنه صار ديناً في مال الميت؛ كذا في البزازية : وفيها من الرهن : قضى دينه وبعضه زيوف وستوقة فرهن شيئاً بالستوقة والزيوف وقال خذه رهناً بما فيه من زيوف وستوق صح في حق الستوق لأنها ليست من الجنس ولا يصح في الزيوف لأنها من الجنس فلا دین اهـ. وقيد بالإقرار بالقبض لأنه لو أقر بألف ولم يبين الجهة ثم ادعى موصولاً أنها زيف لم يقض عليه. واختلف المشايخ قيل أيضاً على الخلاف، وقيل يصدق بالإجماع لأن الجودة تجب في بعض الوجوه لا على البعض فلا تجب بالاحتمال. ولو قال غصبت ألفاً أو أودعني ألفاً إلا أنها زيوف صدق وإن فصل. وعن الإمام أن القرض كالغصب. ولو قال في الغصب والوديعة إلا أنها رصاص أو ستوقة صدق إذا وصل، ولو قال على كر حنطة من ثمن مبيع أو قرض إلا أنه رديء فالقول له، وليس هذا كدعوي الرداءة لأن الرداءة في الحنطة ليست بعيب لأن العيب ما يخلو عنه أصل الفطرة والحنطة قد تكون رديئة بأصل الخلقة فلا يطلق عليه مطلقه على الجيد، ولذا لم يجز شراء البر بدون ذكر الصفة، أقر بقرض عشرة أفلس أو ثمن مبيع ثم ادعى أنها كاسدة لم يصدق وإن وصل. وقالا : يصدق في القرض إذا وصل أما في البيع فلا يصدق عند الثاني في قوله الأول. وقال محمد يصدق في البيع وعليه قيمة المبيع. وكذا الخلاف في قوله علي عشرة ستوقة من قرض أو ثمن المبيع. ولو قال غصبته عشرة أفلس أو أودعني عشرة أفلس ثم قال هي كاسدة صدق المسلم إليه؛ كذا في البزازية. وذكر في القنية مسألة ما إذا أقر بدين ثم ادعى أن بعضه قرض وبعضه ربا أنه يقبل فيه إذا برهن وذكره عبد القادر في الطبقات من الألقاب عن علاء الدين.
Book of Transfer of Debt, Chapter of Arbitration
63
If the heir claims they are counterfeit, the heir is not believed because it has become a debt in the deceased's estate; so in al-Bazzaziyya: And in it from the chapter of pledge: He paid his debt and part of it was counterfeit and base coins, and he pledged something for the base and counterfeit ones and said 'Take it as a pledge for what is in it of counterfeit and base' — it is valid regarding the base coin because it is not of the same type, and not valid regarding the counterfeit because it is of the same type, so no debt. End. And it is conditioned by acknowledgment of receipt because if he acknowledged a thousand without specifying the category then later claimed that it was counterfeit when connected, he is not judged against him. And the scholars differed: some said it is also on the difference, and some said he is believed by consensus because quality is obligatory in some ways not in all, so it is not obligatory by probability. And if he said 'I usurped a thousand' or 'deposited with me a thousand except that they are counterfeit' he is believed even if detailed. And from the Imam that a loan is like usurpation. And if he said in usurpation and deposit 'except they are lead or base coin' he is believed if connected. And if he said 'upon me a kurr of wheat from sale price or loan except that it is poor quality' then his word is accepted, and this is not like a claim of defectiveness because defectiveness in wheat is not a defect since a defect is what is absent from original nature, and wheat may be of poor quality by original creation, so its absolute term does not apply to good quality, and for this reason buying wheat without specifying the quality is not permissible. He acknowledged a loan of ten coins or a sale price then claimed they were worthless — he is not believed even if connected. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is believed in the loan if connected; as for sale, he is not believed according to the second in his first statement. And Muhammad said he is believed in sale and owes the value of what was sold. And similarly the dispute in his saying 'upon me ten base coins from loan or sale price'. And if he said 'I usurped ten coins' or 'deposited with me ten coins' then said 'they are worthless' — the depositor is believed; so in al-Bazzaziyya. And it is mentioned in al-Qunyah the issue of when one acknowledges a debt then claims that part of it is a loan and part is riba — that it is accepted if he proves it, and Abd al-Qadir mentioned it in al-Tabaqat from the titles of Ala al-Din.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, presents several rulings regarding an acknowledgment (iqrar) of debt where the debtor later claims the coins are counterfeit (ziyuf) or defective. The opening rule: if an heir claims that the debt owed to the deceased was in counterfeit coins, the heir is not believed because the debt has already become a claim against the estate. The ruling is from al-Bazzaziyya. The text then discusses a scenario involving a pledge (rahn) where part payment was in counterfeit and part in base coins (sutuqa). The validity of taking such a pledge varies: permissible for base coins (not of the same currency type) but not for counterfeit (same type). The general principle is that if the debtor acknowledges a debt without specifying the quality, then later claims it was of poor quality, his claim is only accepted if he mentioned it at the time of acknowledgment (connected, mawsulan). There is a difference of opinion: some scholars say he is still not believed, but the preferred view is that he is believed by consensus because quality is only obligatory in certain ways. Specific cases: usurpation (ghasb) and deposit (wadi'ah) - if he says 'except they are counterfeit' he is believed if connected. Imam Abu Hanifa equates loan to usurpation. For wheat, if he acknowledges a sale price or loan but says it was poor quality, his word is accepted because poor quality is not a defect in wheat. However, if he acknowledges a loan of coins then claims they were worthless (kasida), he is not believed unless connected; the two companions (Sahibayn) distinguish between loan (believed if connected) and sale (not believed). Muhammad al-Shaybani holds he is believed in sale but must pay the value. The same dispute applies to base coins. Finally, if one acknowledges a debt then claims part is loan part riba, it is accepted only with proof.

Key Terms
زيوف (ziyūf): Counterfeit coins of the same genus as genuine currency.
ستوقة (sutūqa): Base metal coins of a different genus.
كاسدة (kāsida): Worthless coins, no longer in circulation.
موصولاً (mawsūlan): Connected, i.e., mentioned at the time of acknowledgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone acknowledges a loan of coins and later claims they were worthless (kasida) but does not connect the claim?
A) He is believed under all opinions.
B) He is not believed under all opinions.
C) He is believed only according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
D) He is believed only according to Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether a debtor's claim of worthlessness is accepted in loan and sale, but all require the claim to be connected.

Rejection of Acknowledgment and Effect of Later Confirmation
Ruling on acknowledgment rejection and later confirmation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of rejecting an acknowledgment and then confirming it, and distinguish it from contract rescission.

Core Idea
Rejection of an acknowledgment revokes it; later confirmation is a new claim needing proof.

In Hanafi fiqh, an acknowledgment (iqrar) of a debt can be unilaterally rejected by the creditor. If the creditor later confirms the debt after initially rejecting it, the debtor's liability is not automatically revived; the later confirmation is treated as a new claim requiring evidence or the debtor's own acknowledgment. This lesson explains the ruling and how it differs from contract rescission, where both parties' consent is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the passage: a person acknowledges a debt, the creditor rejects, then later confirms. The ruling: 'فلا شيء عليه' (nothing is owed). Understand that the initial acknowledgment is revoked by rejection.
2
Distinguish from contract rescission
Note the comparison: in a sale contract, one party cannot unilaterally rescind because both parties' consent is needed. In acknowledgment, the creditor alone can reject because it is his right alone.
The key difference: contract is bilateral; acknowledgment is unilateral in terms of revocation.
3
Analyze the internal contradiction
Al-Kafi points out a contradiction: earlier in al-Hidayah, the author allowed unilateral rescission in a sale when the buyer denies and collection is impossible. Here he says one cannot rescind alone. Understand the tension.
The contradiction is between two statements by the same author (al-Marghinani).
4
Note the approved resolution
Fath al-Qadir approves the view allowing rescission in cases of impossibility, implying that the general rule (no unilateral rescission) has an exception when performance becomes impossible.
The mufta bihi is that the debtor is free after rejection and later confirmation unless the confirmation is backed by evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن قال لآخر لك علي ألف فرده ثم صدقه فلا شيء عليه) لأن إقراره هو الأول وقد ارتد برد المقر له والثاني دعوى فلا بد من الحجة أو تصديق الخصم بخلاف ما إذا قال اشتريت وأنكر له أن يصدقه لأن أحد العاقدين لا ينفرد بالفسخ كما لا ينفرد بالعقد، والمعنى أنه حقهما فبقي العقد فعمل التصديق أما المقر له فينفرد برد الإقرار فافترقا ؛ كذا الهداية. وناقضه في الكافي بأنه ذكر هنا أن أحد المتعاقدين لا ينفرد بالفسخ وفيما تقدم يعني في مسألة التجاحد قال : ولأنه لما تعذر استيفاء الثمن من المشتري فات رضا البائع فيستبد بالفسخ والترفيق بين كلامه صعب ا هـ . وأقره عليه في فتح القدير بقوله بعده وهو صحيح ويقتضي أنه لو تعذر الاستيفاء مع الإقرار بأن مات ولا بينة أن له أن يفسخ ويستمتع بالجارية
قال
هي
كاسدة صدق المسلم إليه كذا في البزازية. أقول : المسألة السابقة تمت عند قوله «صدق» وقوله المسلم إليه ابتداء مسألة أخرى ذكرها البزازي .
His saying: (And whoever says to another 'You owe me a thousand' and he rejects it then later confirms him, then nothing is upon him) because his acknowledgment is the first and it has been revoked by the rejection of the person acknowledged to, and the second is a claim, so proof or confirmation by the opponent is necessary; unlike if he said 'I bought' and the other denied, for him to confirm him is valid because one of the two contracting parties cannot rescind alone just as he cannot contract alone; and the meaning is that it is their right, so the contract remains and the confirmation takes effect. As for the person acknowledged to, he alone can reject the acknowledgment, so they differ; so in al-Hidayah. And it was contradicted in al-Kafi by the fact that he mentioned here that one of the two contracting parties cannot rescind alone, whereas previously in the issue of denial he said: 'And because when it becomes impossible to collect the price from the buyer, the seller's consent is lost, so he alone rescinds' and reconciling his words is difficult. End. And he approved it in Fath al-Qadir with his following statement: 'And it is correct, and it implies that if collection becomes impossible despite acknowledgment, such as if he dies and there is no evidence, then he may rescind and enjoy the slave-girl.' He said: 'She is worthless, the depositor is believed; so in al-Bazzaziyya.' I say: The previous issue ends at his saying 'believed', and his saying 'the depositor' is the beginning of another issue mentioned by al-Bazzazi.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a person acknowledges a debt (e.g., 'You owe me a thousand') and the creditor (المقر له) rejects it, but later confirms the debt. The ruling is that the debtor is not liable because the initial acknowledgment is considered revoked by the rejection. The subsequent confirmation is treated as a new claim that requires evidence or the opponent's acknowledgment. This is contrasted with a sale contract: if one party claims a sale and the other denies, the denial does not rescind the contract because both parties' consent is needed. However, in acknowledgment, the creditor alone can reject it. The author notes a contradiction (naqda) from al-Kafi: earlier in the issue of jahd (denial), it was stated that if the buyer denies, the seller may unilaterally rescind due to impossibility of collecting the price. The commentator attempts to reconcile but admits difficulty. The approved view in Fath al-Qadir is that the seller may rescind if collection is impossible. The passage ends with a marginal note about a separate issue from al-Bazzaziyya concerning worthless coins.

Key Terms
رد الإقرار (radd al-iqrār): Rejection of an acknowledgment by the person in whose favor it is made.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a person says 'You owe me a thousand' and the creditor rejects, then later confirms, what is the ruling?
A) The debtor must pay the thousand.
B) The debtor is not obligated to pay anything.
C) The debtor must pay only half.
D) The creditor must bring witnesses to prove the debt.

Key Takeaway
Rejection of an acknowledgment revokes the debtor's liability; later confirmation does not revive it automatically but requires new proof.

Reconciling the Apparent Contradiction on Unilateral Rescission in Sale
Resolving an apparent contradiction in al-Hidayah about the seller's right to rescind alone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the apparent contradiction in al-Hidayah regarding the seller's unilateral rescission and state the reconciled ruling according to Hanafi commentators.

Core Idea
The seller may rescind alone when collecting the price is impossible; otherwise, he cannot.

In al-Hidayah, two statements seem contradictory: one says no party can rescind alone, another allows the seller to rescind when the buyer denies. This lesson examines how Hanafi commentators like al-'Inaya and al-Kifaya reconcile these, highlighting the underlying principle of necessity. We also touch on related rulings about quittance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
Read the two statements from al-Hidayah: (1) 'one of the two contracting parties cannot rescind alone' and (2) 'the seller may rescind when collecting the price becomes impossible.' Note the surface tension.
The contradiction is between a general rule and a specific exception.
2
Analyze al-'Inaya's reconciliation
Al-'Inaya argues that the first statement applies when the seller abandons litigation (taraka al-khusumah), and the second when he does not. Consider what this distinction adds.
This suggests the seller's persistence in claiming his right matters.
3
Analyze al-Kifaya's alternative reconciliation
Al-Kifaya holds that the first statement applies when the buyer acknowledges the contract, and the second when the buyer denies (tajahud). The buyer's denial makes collection impossible, triggering the exception.
This frames the exception around the buyer's conduct, not the seller's.
4
Derive the operative rule (mufta bihi)
From the reconciliations, extract the mufta bihi: the seller may rescind unilaterally only when it becomes impossible to collect the price, typically due to the buyer's denial or refusal. Otherwise, rescission requires mutual consent.
Later authorities like Fath al-Qadir prefer this view.
5
Apply to related rulings on quittance
The passage also discusses when quittance (ibra') can be rescinded by rejection. Understand that the same principle of 'necessity' and 'completion of the act' governs these rules.
Exceptions: ibra' requested by the debtor, and ibra' of a guarantor, are not rescinded by rejection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلا بد من الحجة) قال في الحواشي السعدية : كيف تقبل حجته وهو متناقض في دعواه
فسخاً.
والوجه ما قدمه أو لا ا هـ . وأجاب عنه في العناية بأن لا مناقضة لأنه إنما حكم أولاً بكونه من جهته لا مطلقاً أو لأن كلامه الأوّل فيما إذا ترك البائع الخصومة والثاني فيما إذا لم يتركها. وقوله «فلا شيء عليه أي بسبب الإقرار أما إذا برهن المقر له أو صدقه خصمه فإنه يلزم المقر كما في الهداية. وسيأتي رده في البزازية والحاصل أن كل شيء يكون الحق لهما جميعاً إذا رجع المنكر إلى التصديق قبل أن يصدقه الآخر على إنكاره فهو جائز كالبيع والنكاح .

تأمل في جوابه اهـ. واستشكله المؤلف أيضاً فيما يأتي في هذه السوادة قوله : (وأجاب عنه في العناية الخ) وفي الحواشي اليعقوبية قال صاحب الكفاية : لا تناقض بين كلاميه فيحتاج إلى التوفيق لأن مراده بقوله «لأن أحد المتعاقدين لا ينفرد بالفسخ فيما إذا كان الآخر على العقد معترفاً به كما إذا قال أحدهما اشتريت وأنكر الآخر لا يكون إنكاره فسخاً للعقد إذ لا يتم به الفسخ، وفيما إذا قال أحدهما اشتريت مني هذه الجارية وأنكر فالمدعي للعقد هو البائع والمشتري ينكر العقد والبائع بانفراده على العقد فيستبد بفسخه أيضاً وفيه كلام، وهو أن الظاهر من قوله فيما سبق ولأنه لما تعذر الخ» كون مجرد استقلال البائع في الفسخ لتعذر استيفاء الثمن دليلاً مستقلاً لحل الوطء بدون اعتبار كون إنكار المشتري فسخاً من جانبه حتى لو تعذر الاستيفاء مع عدم الإنكار لا يستبد بالفسخ أيضاً، ويدل على هذا قول صدر الشريعة في تعريفه حل الوطء لا سيما إذا جحد المشتري الخ» كما لا يخفى، بل غاية ما يمكن في التوفيق أن يقال : إن مراده فيما سبق استبداد البائع بالفسخ لضرورة تعذر استيفاء الثمن ووجوب دفع الضرر هنا لا ضرورة للمقر له بالشراء إلى الفسخ فلا يستبد به، فمراده من قوله ههنا «لأن أحد العاقدين لا ينفرد بالفسخ الخ ) عدم الانفراد عند عدم الضرورة فلا تنافض لكنه بعيد لا يخفى فليتأمل اهـ. قوله : ( وسيأتي رده في البزازية) أي رد قوله أما إن برهن المقر له وهو ما قدمناه عن السعدية قوله : (والحاصل أن كل شيء الخ) وجد في بعض النسخ مقدماً على قوله وقوله فلا شيء عليه قوله : (قيد بكون التصديق بعد الرد الخ) قال الرملي وفي البزازية الإقرار والإبراء لا
His saying: (So evidence is necessary) said in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya: How can his evidence be accepted while he is contradictory in his claim of rescission. The correct opinion is what was presented first. End. And he answered it in al-'Inaya that there is no contradiction because he first ruled that it is from his side not absolutely, or because his first statement is when the seller leaves the litigation and the second when he does not leave it. And his saying 'so nothing is upon him' means due to the acknowledgment; but if the acknowledged person proves it or his opponent confirms him, then it is binding on the acknowledger as in al-Hidayah. And its rejection will come in al-Bazzaziyya. The conclusion: Everything that is the right of both, if the denier returns to confirmation before the other confirms his denial, it is permissible, like sale and marriage. And everything that is the right of one, like gift, charity, and acknowledgment, his acknowledgment after that does not benefit him; so in al-Qunyah. And it is conditioned that the confirmation be after rejection, because if he first accepted the acknowledgment then rejected it, it is not rescinded. Similarly, quittance from debt and its gift, because it is completed by acceptance. And similarly, if he endows a person and he accepts then rejects, it is not rescinded, and if he rejects before acceptance, it is rescinded as in al-Is'af. Then know that quittance is rescinded by rejection except when the debtor says 'Grant me quittance' and he grants it, then it is not rescinded as in al-Bazzaziyya. Similarly, quittance of a guarantor is not rescinded by rejection. So the exceptions are two issues. Just as their saying that quittance does not depend on acceptance excludes quittance from currency exchange and salam, for it depends on acceptance to void them as we presented in the chapter of salam. Then know that if he claims that he acknowledged the property from which he quitted him, if he said 'He granted me quittance and I accepted it', the acknowledgment is not valid because the rejection after acceptance is not valid; and if he did not say 'and I accepted', the acknowledgment is valid because quittance can be rejected, so it becomes void and the acknowledgment is valid. And the author also questioned it later in this marginal note his saying: (And he answered in al-'Inaya etc.) And in al-Hawashi al-Ya'qubiyya, the author of al-Kifaya said: There is no contradiction between his two statements, so there is need for reconciliation because his meaning by his saying 'one of the two contracting parties cannot rescind alone' is when the other is acknowledging the contract; as when one says 'I bought' and the other denies, his denial is not a rescission of the contract since rescission is not completed by it. And when one says 'You bought this slave-girl from me' and the other denies, the claimant of the contract is the seller, and the buyer denies the contract, and the seller alone can rescind because he is the claimant. And there is discussion in it: The apparent meaning of his earlier statement 'And because when it becomes impossible etc.' is that the mere independence of the seller in rescission due to impossibility of collecting the price is an independent proof for allowing intercourse without considering whether the buyer's denial is a rescission from his side, so that if collection becomes impossible without denial, he does not rescind alone either. And this is supported by the statement of Sadr al-Shari'a in his definition: 'The permissibility of intercourse, especially if the buyer denies etc.' as is not hidden. Rather, the best reconciliation is to say: His earlier meaning is the seller's independence in rescission due to the necessity of impossibility of collecting the price and the obligation to remove harm; here, there is no necessity for the acknowledged person to rescind the purchase, so he does not do it alone. So his meaning by his saying here 'one of the two contracting parties cannot rescind alone' is non-independence when there is no necessity, so there is no contradiction. But it is far from clear, so reflect. End. His saying: (And its rejection will come in al-Bazzaziyya) i.e., the rejection of his statement 'but if the acknowledged person proves' which we presented from al-Sa'diyya. His saying: (And the conclusion that everything etc.) Found in some copies preceded by his saying 'so nothing is upon him'. Commentary
This dense passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses an apparent contradiction in al-Hidayah regarding the seller's right to unilaterally rescind a sale. The first statement says one party cannot rescind alone; the second says the seller may rescind if collecting the price becomes impossible. Commentators offer various reconciliations: the first statement applies when the buyer acknowledges the contract and is merely litigating; the second when the buyer denies the contract entirely. Another view: the seller may rescind only when collection is impossible, and the buyer's denial is not a rescission. The passage then discusses related rulings: quittance (ibra') from debt is normally rescinded by rejection, but exceptions exist (e.g., when the debtor requests quittance). If a person acknowledges a debt and later accepts quittance, his acknowledgment may be valid if he did not explicitly accept the quittance. The text advises careful study due to the complexity.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibrā'): Quittance or release from a debt.
تجاحد (tajāḥud): Mutual denial (of a contract).
تعذر الاستيفاء (ta'addhur al-istifa'): Impossibility of collecting (the price).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciliation in al-'Inaya, when can the seller unilaterally rescind the sale?
A) Whenever the buyer delays payment.
B) Only when it becomes impossible to collect the price.
C) Only if the buyer openly denies the contract.
D) The seller can never rescind alone.

Key Takeaway
The seller's right to rescind alone is conditional upon impossibility of collecting the price, not absolute; Hanafi commentaries reconcile apparent contradictions by contextualizing the statements.
